Saved files can also be imported into Google Earth, Microsoft MapPoint or Streets and Trips and many other apps that read GPX files.\r\n\r\nDownload the app on your Windows 10 PC/tablet AND your phone.  The app and GPX files are compatible.\r\n\r\nImport/export placemarks to a local file or cloud storage file.  The files are saved in clear text XML format.  Edit them and resave in any text editor.\r\n\r\n*Important: when running the GPS, if you need to log the data be sure to start saving the data right away, that way if the app or phone/tablet happens to crash you will still have almost all the data minus a minute or two.\r\n\r\nSaved GPX files can also be used with FreeLogBook.biz to help keep electronic logbook and track mobiles within a company.  http://www.freelogbook.biz/home/\r\n\r\nNow works under lock screen or in the background!\r\n\r\nThis app is designed to be used with the GPS/GNSS Geolocation device built into some newer tablets and Windows phones. No pop-up or full-screen ads. Provide best user experience.\r\n\r\nThe classic game of whist is a plain-trick game without bidding for 4 players in fixed partnerships. There are four players in two fixed partnerships. Partners sit facing each other. A standard 52 card pack is used. The cards in each suit rank from highest to lowest: A K Q J 10 9 8 7 6 5 4 3 2.\r\n\r\nThe player to the dealer's left leads to the first trick. Any card may be led. The other players, in clockwise order, each play a card to the trick. Players must follow suit by playing a card of the same suit as the card led if they can; a player with no card of the suit led may play any card. The trick is won by the highest trump in it - or if it contains no trump, by the highest card of the suit led. The winner of a trick leads to the next.\r\n\r\nWhen all 13 tricks have been played, the side which won more tricks scores 1 point for each trick they won in excess of 6.
